GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 52

GT (fixed):  
\[
f(x,t)=0.422619160916855\sin t\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly:
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term with amplitude \(0.4226...\) and no other \(t\)-dependence,
- a linear-in-\(x\) term,
- an \(x e^{-|x|}\) term (note the **minus** in the exponent and the **Abs**).

Also, because \(x\) can be negative, \(e^{-|x|}\) cannot be replaced by \(e^{+|x|}\) or \(e^{-x}\) globally.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to reproduce exactly these three terms and eliminate all extra terms.

---

### 1.
Has \(c0 x\), \(c1\cos(t+c2)\), \(c3 x e^{c4|x|}\), plus a product of cosines.  
- Set product term \(c5=0\).  
- Choose \(c4=-1\) to get \(e^{-|x|}\).  
- Cos can become sin by phase shift: \(\cos(t+c2)=\sin t\) with \(c2=\pi/2\).  
Then set \(c1=0.422619...\), \(c0=-1.153571...\), \(c3=-1.153571...\). Works. **Match.**

### 2.
Same core pieces as (1) but extra term \(c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(c7 x+c8)\cos(t+c9)\).  
Set \(c5=0\) to remove it; remaining can match exactly as in (1). **Match.**

### 3.
Extra term \(c5\cos(c6 e^{c7 t})\). Set \(c5=0\). Remaining matches as in (1). **Match.**

### 4.
Has \(c0 x\), \(c1\cos(t+c2)\), \(c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\), and \(c6 x e^{c7|x|}\).  
We only need one sinusoid in \(t\). We can:
- set \(c3=0\) and use the cosine term (phase-shifted) as \(\sin t\), or set \(c1=0\) and use the sine term with \(c4=1,c5=0\).  
Also set \(c7=-1\). Then choose coefficients to match. **Match.**

### 5.
Has constant offset \(c1\) and \(x e^{c6 |x|^{c7}}\).  
Set \(c1=0\). Need \(|x|^{c7}=|x|\) so set \(c7=1\), and \(c6=-1\).  
Sin term can be \(\sin(t)\) by \(c3=1,c4=0\). Linear term via \(c0\). **Match.**

### 6.
Same as (5) but already \(x e^{c6|x|}\). Set \(c1=0\), \(c4=1,c3=0\) (or appropriate), \(c6=-1\). **Match.**

### 7.
Exactly three needed structures: \(c0 x + c1\cos(c2 t+c3)+c4 x e^{c5|x|}\).  
Set \(c2=1\), choose \(c3=\pi/2\) to make cosine into \(\sin t\), set \(c5=-1\), and match coefficients. **Match.**

### 8.
Contains \(c0 x^3\) and \(x e^{c6|x|^{c7}}\).  
Set \(c0=0\). Set \(c7=1,c6=-1\). Cos term phase-shift to sin. Linear term via \(c1\). **Match.**

### 9.

### 40.
Has \(c4 x^{c5} e^{c6|x|}\) plus \(c2 x e^{c3|x|}\) and cosine-in-time, but **no pure linear \(x\)** unless one of those terms becomes exactly linear.  
- If \(c3=0\), then \(x e^{0}=x\) gives linear, but then the other term would need to become \(x e^{-|x|}\). That would require \(x^{c5}e^{c6|x|}=x e^{-|x|}\) ⇒ \(c5=1,c6=-1\), which is possible. Then we’d have both linear and \(x e^{-|x|}\) available. Also cosine can phase shift to sin. So actually this **can** match by setting:
  - \(c3=0\) and \(c2=-1.153571...\) (linear term),
  - \(c5=1,c6=-1\) and \(c4=-1.153571...\) (the \(x e^{-|x|}\) term),
  - \(c0=0.422619...\), \(c1=\pi/2\) (cos→sin).  
**Match.**

### 41.

### 43.

### 45.

### 46.

Note that sin(t) = cos(t - π/2) = cos(-(π/2 - t)) = cos(π/2 - t), so sin(t) can be written as cos(c + t) with c = -π/2.
